### Post by ezsit on 2008-08-21
> LinuxMint is much more than Ubuntu with more programs

I've used LinuxMint from Bianca up to the most current, and LinuxMint really is just Ubuntu with some customization and extra utilities thrown in. It's a very nice mix of programs and works well most of the time. 

I have never found a version of LinuxMint to be quite as stable as the corresponding version of Ubuntu (much like Ubuntu is not nearly as stable as Debian), but the further you remove the source from the purists, the more apt you are to get breakage.

All this being said, I still think LinuxMint has its' place and I never suggested that LinuxMint did not have a right be developed. To each their own. However, to say that LinuxMint is somehow independent from Ubuntu (or Debian) and can be a self-supporting distribution is simply not the case. Debian and Ubuntu developers provide 99% of the LinuxMint codebase, and without those people, LinuxMint would be forced to re-base or develop from scratch. So to say that LinuxMint can ever "exceed" Ubuntu (and that Ubuntu could ever "exceed" Debian) is utter nonsense.

---

### Post by ezsit on 2008-08-21
> Ubuntu which actually contributes a lot back to Debian and at least isn't a direct fork / distro with a bunch of home-made tools & preinstalled programs, it's more or less on the "parallel

Ubuntu is taken straight from the Debian Sid branch, pieced together and tested for six months, then released as stable. Sure, Ubuntu customizes the artwork, boot-up process, and added a handful of utilities, but all-in-all, Ubuntu is releasing a customized, working snapshot of Debian Sid every six months, with updates, security patches, and support if you want to pay.

Don't get me wrong, I use Kubuntu everyday at home and have Ubuntu installed on my backup machine. I've been running Ubuntu ever since version 5.04 and I think its great.

### Post by ben2talk on 2008-08-30
> **Eclipse. said:**
> It comes with codecs preinstalled which you can easily install in ubuntu using the restricted-extras package.

IMHO - After reading, they have 'Mint Tools' which is the only major difference - however, after installing the 'Elyssa' Mint-Menu I can tell you it's basically the same as 'Slab Menu' for gnome. Reasonably nice layout, however I nearly always use the non-menu access (gnome-do, alt+f2, alt+f3 etc) but it has the advantage that it doesn't take up the space of the 'Menu bar' (always being stuck with the length of the titles Applications-Places-System). It's ok, but nothing to write home about.

Next comes the 'Software Portal' which is available as a .deb file (they all are) and freely installable in Ubuntu 

This opens a small gtk front end with tabs for 'LinuxMint/GetDeb.net/APT' and a shortcut link to open in a browser 'Linx Mint Software portal', 'GetDeb Portal' and for APT there's the LinuxMint repository and the Ubuntu repository.

Nice, I have it in Ubuntu gnome, so I don't need to switch now do I? :)) I did notice a great number of 'Donate' buttons littering Mint, and I feel that there is another story there. Perhaps they're preparing for problems mixing Open Source with other people's property.

Ubuntu got it right by leaving it out, and simply needs to ensure it's easy to install. Sure it's simpler, like supermarkets with no checkouts.

IMHO	In My Humble Opinion
IMHO	In My Hesitating Opinion
IMHO	In My Highest Opinion
IMHO	In My Holy Opinion

in the address bar. Search for "browser.search" and look for a string that has mint specific settings.

### Post by Wiebelhaus on 2008-09-01
> [http://www.linuxmint.com/start/](http://www.linuxmint.com/start/)

This is what your search engine is set to.

You want traditional google , it's a search engine plug in > /usr/share/firefox/searchplugins/google.xml or > /usr/lib/firefox/pluginsor best bet > /usr/lib/firefox-3.0.1/searchpluginsif your running the newest version of firefox it will be in /usr/lib/***

Delete the stupid thing ,linux mint's is called > /usr/share/firefox/searchplugins/google_image.xml

### Post by Zero Prime on 2008-09-02
As per the LinuxMint blog

Go to [https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3682](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3682)
Install the addon and restart Firefox
Go to google [http://www.google.com](http://www.google.com)
Right click in google search bar and select “add to search bar”
Left-click arrow at left side of firefox search combo
Select “manage search engine”
You should find google at the bottom of the list
Move it to the top

This will fix the problem.

### Post by estyles on 2008-09-04
I run Linux Mint primarily, and the only thing that I miss when I try out other distros is the Mint Menu.  If I can get Arch running smoothly (right now, I can NOT), I'll try to find a way to use the Mint Menu instead of the default Gnome menu.  Other than that, to me Mint is just Ubuntu with a nicer theme.  MintInstall (why isn't it called MIntstall?) and MintUpdate don't add enough for me to really care about them, and the pre-installed codecs aren't really necessary - it only takes a few clicks or one line of typing.

The fact that Mint doesn't include a workspace switcher on the default desktop is enough for me to recommend Ubuntu to friends instead (as piddling a detail as that is)...  they are virtually identical in my mind, and a newbie that doesn't see a workspace switcher may never discover how useful it is to have different desktops.

### Post by namegame on 2008-09-10

---

### Post by 67GTA on 2008-09-10
It will still be based on Ubuntu for the foreseeable future. Clem has dabbled with a Fedora and Debian test version just for fun, but has stated he has no plans to switch bases. Each version of Mint is based on the previous version of Mint, and then all of the packages are updated to the latest Ubuntu package base. It is not a Ubuntu remaster. Mint 5 is based on Mint 4, with Hardy's package base. It has been this way since Edgy. Clem has created a Mint backports repository to keep the most important packages in Mint 5 updated to the latest Mint version until the next LTS. Clem has not stated for sure which apps will go in to the backports repo yet though. So i guess Mint 5 will be a semi-rolling release:)

---

### Post by Vorian Grey on 2008-09-24
> In computer science, the kernel is the central component of most computer operating systems (OS). Its responsibilities include managing the system's resources (the communication between hardware and software components).[1] As a basic component of an operating system, a kernel provides the lowest-level abstraction layer for the resources (especially memory, processors and I/O devices) that application software must control to perform its function. It typically makes these facilities available to application processes through inter-process communication mechanisms and system calls.

[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kernel_(computer_science](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kernel_(computer_science))

Maybe that will help you understand it a little better.

### Post by Therion on 2008-09-24
> **PT.Linn.A said:**
> I am still looking for a clear reason to install Mint versus Ubuntu. Or, some other Linux Distro. There seem to be SOOOO many.
Well I think it's safe to say that everyone has their own ideas about why the prefer a particular distro over another.

For me, I look at hardware recognition first.  Pretty obvious.  I ain't gonna fuss with hardware recognition.  If it's not there, that's it.  Game over.  Next distro, please.

The next thing I look at is the package manager and, IMO, you can't beat Synaptic.  Yast (*a la* OpenSuse) runs a close second in my book.  

I then look at the repositories for that distro and simply put "bigger is better" (huge generalization but what can ya do?).  

The DE (Desktop Environment) is huge for me too.  I just can't do KDE.  I'm a Gnome guy and KDE is a deal-breaker for me.  

The last thing I care about (meaning I couldn't care less about it) is the GUI (theme, etc) since that's about the easiest aspect of any distro to totally customize.

> **PT.Linn.A said:**
> Is Mint truly its own entity? Or, is just the radical black sheep of the Ubuntu family?
I wouldn't call it "radical" OR a "black sheep".  It's an Ubuntu "fork".  Just as Ubuntu forked from Debian.  Ultimate Edition is another "fork"; it's Ubuntu-based but it's been heavily overhauled from the ground up and constitutes it's own distro, IMO; just as Mint does.

---

The next thing I look at is the package manager and, IMO, you can't beat Synaptic.  Yast (*a la* OpenSuse) runs a close second in my book.

### Post by Therion on 2008-09-24
> **PT.Linn.A said:**
> This actually helped. It has given me direction. Sorta felt like I was floundering a bit. But, now I have some definitive things I can look for.

Yikes! that I didn't come up with my own list as yours above. I guess I'm just a little intimidated with the whole complete switch from MS.
If you're feeling totally overwhelmed by all the different distros out there (i.e. Kid in a Candy Store Syndrome) allow me to suggest you try three different distros:

[INDENT]Ubuntu
Fedora
OpenSuse[/INDENT]

Why those three?  Because they are three of the most popular distros "out there".  Between those three you will experience, I think it's safe to say, a very broad spectrum of what Linux has to offer.  So there, now I've pinned it down for you.  :)

Secondly, don't feel you have to jump out of one operating system and into another.  You can use LiveCD's until you've narrowed things down to one OS in particular that's really working for you.  Then install it and dual-boot between your new distro of choice AND WinXP or Vista or whatever.

Most of all though... Relax.  Don't worry; have fun and use what works.  When you're ready to take a step come back and ask for help if you need it.  

As I'm fond of saying...  "It's more process than event."

---

### Post by Therion on 2008-09-24
> **PT.Linn.A said:**
> Fantastic! Truly good advice. Only have one question remaining before I go on my Linux Quest/Adventure. And, I'm not sure that my actual question is going to be worded correctly. So, I'm hoping that it reads the way I intend it to.

What about trying the different variations of each Distro? ie Mint, Ultimate Edition, etc. And, are the variations supported through the main site of their "fork"?
I think I understand what you're asking; and if I do the answer is (pretty much) yes.  If a disto is a fork (for instance both Ultimate and Mint are Ubuntu forks) what holds true for Ubuntu would hold true for any distro that "forked" from it.  

Mostly.  

I can't think of a specific example where it wouldn't but I'm not going to say it's impossible for a conflict to happen; I just can't think of one off the top of my head.  For instance I run Ultimate Edition on my machine, but I treat it like a plain-vanilla Ubuntu install.  That works for Ultimate Edition (treating it as if it were plain-vanilla Ubuntu).  I can't say that it would work 100% of the time with say, Linux Mint.  Most likely, yes, but I'm not going to promise it.

Does that answer your question?

As for trying distro's like Mint, if it appeals to you, go for it!  My previous post was full of *suggestions*.  That's all they are...  If a particular distro jumps out at you and looks really good, by all means... Fire up a LiveCD and take it for a test spin!!  

The whole Linux/open source movement, its *cornerstone*, is CHOICE.  

Get out there and start exercising your power... of choice.

---

### Post by Down8ve on 2008-09-26
I've been toying with LinuxMint 64-bit during the past two days, and am very impressed.  PCLinux was nice, but I am shying away from the one-man distros for obvious reasons.  I've learned that Ubuntu-based systems, like Ultimate Edition, Klikit, and Mint offer a better user experience for the average user than anything else I've tried (openSuSE, Fedora, Mandriva).  

While Ultimate looked pretty good, there were issues with certain included apps that would not launch and such.  For me, that's a warning that other problems may be in store.

Opensuse was very cool, but it is very confusing to have four different controls that appear to do the same thing.  They've got a good thing going, but still, printing to a Windows networked printer?  Ouch!  Sharing files?  How many buttons must I push for that one?  And the "help" they offer....please!

Mint was not the distro I really wanted to run, but it does work.  Easily.  The Mint and Ubuntu forums supply easy answers.  Multimedia just works.  I've a bad download of the KDE version, so was unable to try it (Again, I'm using a release candidate of the x64 version, which uses Gnome).

Klikit looks fantastic, but like PCLOS, is in the hands of one fella and is now in a holding pattern.

Actually, a light year is also a measure of time, equal to a year, because time is equivalent to space, and there is an equivalency between a year and the distance that light travels in a year.

So the article is two years old = the article is two light years old = two light years in the software industry (assuming that light years in one industry are equivalent to light years in another...  maybe there's an exchange rate?).

So, the previous post is technically correct...  :lolflag:

### Post by scorp123 on 2008-11-18
> **estyles said:**
> Actually, a light year is also a measure of time  Nonsense.
[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_year](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_year)

1 LY = 9.461 * 10^12 km

> A light-year or light year (symbol: ly) is a **_unit of length_**, equal to just under ten trillion kilometres. As defined by the International Astronomical Union (which is the body which has the jurisdictional authority to promulgate the definition), a light-year is the distance that light travels in a vacuum in one Julian year.

---

### Post by estyles on 2008-11-19
> **scorp123 said:**
> Nonsense.
[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_year](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_year)

1 LY = 9.461 * 10^12 km

I suppose you've never heard of relativity?  By the theory of relativity, space and time are equivalent (making up 4-dimensional space-time), so any measure of length is also a measure of time.  The conversion between length and time is c.  So 1 year = 9.461 X 10^12 km.  Exactly the length of a light-year (for obvious reasons).  1 year = 1 light year.

### Post by clemyeats on 2008-12-16
Hi, 

I just dropped here to see people's reaction (if any) about Felicia but I find the little argument about time == length extremely amusing. 

The guy is right though. From a machist point of view...

time --> money --> women
length --> .... well, anyway... hum!  

On a more serious note, and although it is indeed a unit of length, it's very often used for two different purposes: 

- To describe the minimum amount of time it would take us to go to some point of the universe. 

- To describe how old what we're seing in the universe actually is. 

So even though it's ridiculous to say things like time=length and even though LY is indeed a measure of length it is commonly used to express a length of time (simply because it's not just a length, it's a length associated to a maximum speed value and to the speed with which travels our perception of what's around us). 

Scorp123, nice to see you again ;)

Clem
PS: By the way, should we say "length" or "distance"?
